If H has dimension 1 (|H| = p): X + Y is a union of cosets of H. |X + Y| ≥ |X + H| + |Y + H| - p. Each of |X + H| and |Y + H| is a multiple of p. 

If H has dimension 2 (|H| = p^2): X + Y is a union of cosets of H, so |X + Y| ≥ |X + H| + |Y + H| - p^2. Each of |X + H| and |Y + H| is a multiple of p^2.

If H has dimension 3: H = F_p^3, so X + Y = F_p^3. Then |X + Y| = p^3, which is what we want.

So for X + Y ≠ F_p^3, H has dimension at most 2.
